                 <section class="hh hi hj eg hk">
                  <h2 class="hl hm hn be b ho hp hq ej hr" id="2d40">
                   INTUITIVE AUDIO DEEP LEARNING SERIES
                  </h2>
                  <div class="">
                   <h1 class="hs ht hn be hu hv hw hx hy hz ia ib ic id ie if ig ih ii ij ik il hd" id="a7d2">
                    <a class="ex ca" href="/audio-deep-learning-made-simple-sound-classification-step-by-step-cebc936bbe5?source=collection_home---------0----------------------------" rel="noopener">
                     Audio Deep Learning Made Simple: Sound Classification, Step-by-Step
                    </a>
                   </h1>
                  </div>
                  <div class="">
                   <h2 class="im ht hn be b in io ip iq ir is it iu iv iw ix iy iz ej" id="ed64">
                    An end-to-end example and architecture for audio deep learning’s foundational application scenario, in plain English.
                   </h2>
                  </div>
                  <figure class="ja jb jc jd paragraph-image">
                   <a href="https://towardsdatascience.com/audio-deep-learning-made-simple-sound-classification-step-by-step-cebc936bbe5?source=collection_home---------0----------------------------">
                    <div class="je">
                     <div class="jj ai ar jk">
                      <div class="jl jm ai">
                       <div class="fq jf ff ft fp hc v jg jh ji">
                        <img alt="" class="ff ft fp hc v jn jo jp" height="667" role="presentation" src="https://miro.medium.com/max/60/0*Aoo5Ijq3sfHSIq-A?q=20" width="1000"/>
                       </div>
                       <img alt="" class="fq jf ff ft fp hc v c" height="667" role="presentation" width="1000"/>
                       <noscript>
                        <img alt="" class="ff ft fp hc v" height="667" role="presentation" sizes="1000px" src="https://miro.medium.com/max/2000/0*Aoo5Ijq3sfHSIq-A" srcset="https://miro.medium.com/max/552/0*Aoo5Ijq3sfHSIq-A 276w, https://miro.medium.com/max/1104/0*Aoo5Ijq3sfHSIq-A 552w, https://miro.medium.com/max/1280/0*Aoo5Ijq3sfHSIq-A 640w, https://miro.medium.com/max/1456/0*Aoo5Ijq3sfHSIq-A 728w, https://miro.medium.com/max/1632/0*Aoo5Ijq3sfHSIq-A 816w, https://miro.medium.com/max/1808/0*Aoo5Ijq3sfHSIq-A 904w, https://miro.medium.com/max/1984/0*Aoo5Ijq3sfHSIq-A 992w, https://miro.medium.com/max/2000/0*Aoo5Ijq3sfHSIq-A 1000w" width="1000"/>
                       </noscript>
                      </div>
                     </div>
                    </div>
                   </a>
                   <figcaption class="jq dd jr go gp js jt be b ho bg ej">
                    Photo by
                    <a class="ex ju" href="https://unsplash.com/@brucemars?utm_source=medium&amp;utm_medium=referral" rel="noopener nofollow">
                     bruce mars
                    </a>
                    on
                    <a class="ex ju" href="https://unsplash.com?utm_source=medium&amp;utm_medium=referral" rel="noopener nofollow">
                     Unsplash
                    </a>
                   </figcaption>
                  </figure>
                  <p class="jv jw hn jx b iq hw jy is hz jz ka kb kc kd ke kf kg kh ki dh kj hh hd" id="a036">
                   Sound Classification is one of the most widely used applications in Audio Deep Learning. It involves learning to classify sounds and to predict the category of that sound. This type of problem can be applied to many practical scenarios e.g. classifying music clips to identify the genre of the music, or classifying short utterances by a set of speakers to identify the speaker based on the voice.
                  </p>
                  <p class="jv jw hn jx b iq hw jy is hz jz ka kb kc kd ke kf kg kh ki kk kj hh hd" id="61b3">
                   In this article, we will walk through a simple demo application so as to understand the approach used to solve such audio classification problems. …
                  </p>
                 </section>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="kl ai">
               <a class="ex ey cd ce cf cg ch ci cj bp ez fa ck fb fc" href="/audio-deep-learning-made-simple-sound-classification-step-by-step-cebc936bbe5?readmore=1&amp;source=collection_home---------0----------------------------" rel="noopener">
                <p class="be b bf bg fy">
                 Read more
                 <!-- -->
                 <!-- -->
                 · 12 min read
                </p>
               </a>
              </div>
              <div class="km n o co">
               <div class="n o">
                <div class="n o">
                 <div class="ai ar kn ko kp kq kr">
                  <span>
                   <a class="ex ey cd ce cf cg ch ci cj bp ez fa ck fb fc" href="https://medium.com/m/signin?actionUrl=https%3A%2F%2Fmedium.com%2F_%2Fvote%2Ftowards-data-science%2Fcebc936bbe5&amp;operation=register&amp;redirect=https%3A%2F%2Ftowardsdatascience.com%2F&amp;source=collection_home-----cebc936bbe5----0-----------------clap_preview-----------" rel="noopener">
                    <div class="ci ks kt ku fk kv kw kx r ky kz">
                     <svg aria-label="clap" height="25" viewbox="0 0 25 25" width="25">
                      <g fill-rule="evenodd">
                       <path d="M11.74 0l.76 2.97.76-2.97zM14.81 3.78l1.84-2.56-1.42-.47zM8.38 1.22l1.84 2.56L9.8.75zM20.38 21.62a5.11 5.11 0 0 1-3.16 1.61l.49-.45c2.88-2.89 3.45-5.98 1.69-9.21l-1.1-1.94-.96-2.02c-.31-.67-.23-1.18.25-1.55a.84.84 0 0 1 .66-.16c.34.05.66.28.88.6l2.85 5.02c1.18 1.97 1.38 5.12-1.6 8.1M7.1 21.1l-5.02-5.02a1 1 0 0 1 .7-1.7 1 1 0 0 1 .72.3l2.6 2.6a.44.44 0 0 0 .63-.62L4.1 14.04l-1.75-1.75a1 1 0 1 1 1.41-1.41l4.15 4.15a.44.44 0 0 0 .63 0 .44.44 0 0 0 0-.62L4.4 10.26 3.22 9.08a1 1 0 0 1 0-1.4 1.02 1.02 0 0 1 1.41 0l1.18 1.16L9.96 13a.44.44 0 0 0 .62 0 .44.44 0 0 0 0-.63L6.43 8.22a.99.99 0 0 1-.3-.7.99.99 0 0 1 .3-.7 1 1 0 0 1 1.41 0l7 6.98a.44.44 0 0 0 .7-.5l-1.35-2.85c-.31-.68-.23-1.19.25-1.56a.85.85 0 0 1 .66-.16c.34.06.66.28.88.6L18.63 14c1.57 2.88 1.07 5.54-1.55 8.16a5.62 5.62 0 0 1-5.06 1.65 9.35 9.35 0 0 1-4.93-2.72zM11 5.98l2.56 2.56c-.5.6-.56 1.41-.15 2.28l.26.56-4.25-4.25a.98.98 0 0 1-.12-.45 1 1 0 0 1 .29-.7 1.02 1.02 0 0 1 1.41 0zm8.89 2.06c-.38-.56-.9-.92-1.49-1.01a1.74 1.74 0 0 0-1.34.33c-.38.29-.61.65-.71 1.06a2.1 2.1 0 0 0-1.1-.56 1.78 1.78 0 0 0-.99.13l-2.64-2.64a1.88 1.88 0 0 0-2.65 0 1.86 1.86 0 0 0-.48.85 1.89 1.89 0 0 0-2.67-.01 1.87 1.87 0 0 0-.5.9c-.76-.75-2-.75-2.7-.04a1.88 1.88 0 0 0 0 2.66c-.3.12-.61.29-.87.55a1.88 1.88 0 0 0 0 2.66l.62.62a1.88 1.88 0 0 0-.9 3.16l5.01 5.02c1.6 1.6 3.52 2.64 5.4 2.96a7.16 7.16 0 0 0 1.18.1c1.03 0 2-.25 2.9-.7A5.9 5.9 0 0 0 21 22.24c3.34-3.34 3.08-6.93 1.74-9.17l-2.87-5.04z">
                       </path>
                      </g>
                     </svg>

                    Consciousness and AI
                   </a>
                  </h1>
                 </div>
                 <div class="">
                  <h2 class="im ht hn be b in io ip iq ir is it iu iv iw ix iy iz ej" id="0740">
                   Georg Northoff explains how a good theory of consciousness could lead to better AI
                  </h2>
                 </div>
                 <figure class="dh jb">
                  <div class="jj ai ar">
                   <div class="nd jm ai">
                   </div>
                  </div>
                  <figcaption class="jq dd jr go gp js jt be b ho bg ej">
                   <a class="ex ju" href="https://podcasts.apple.com/ca/podcast/towards-data-science/id1470952338?mt=2" rel="noopener nofollow">
                    APPLE
                   </a>
                   |
                   <a class="ex ju" href="https://www.google.com/podcasts?feed=aHR0cHM6Ly9hbmNob3IuZm0vcy8zNmI0ODQ0L3BvZGNhc3QvcnNz" rel="noopener nofollow">

                 <p class="jv jw hn jx b iq ne hw jy is nf hz jz ka ng kb kc kd nh ke kf kg ni kh ki kj hh hd" id="f429">
                  For the past decade, progress in AI has mostly been driven by deep learning — a field of research that draws inspiration directly from the structure and function of the human brain. By drawing an analogy between brains and computers, we’ve been able to build computer vision, natural language and other predictive systems that would have been inconceivable just ten years ago.
                 </p>
                 <p class="jv jw hn jx b iq hw jy is hz jz ka kb kc kd ke kf kg kh ki kk kj hh hd" id="cc5a">

                   </a>

                 <p class="jv jw hn jx b iq hw jy is hz jz ka kb kc kd ke kf kg kh ki mq kj hh hd" id="5f0e">
                  While Big Sleep is still the Big Hype on reddit, I decided to take another look at open questions in the context of deep dreaming on consecutive frames, i.e. videos. Inspired by preceding work, such as
                  <a class="ex ju" href="https://github.com/samim23/DeepDreamAnim" rel="noopener nofollow">
                   this Caffe implementation
                  </a>
                  , I wanted to include more recent insights on single class dreaming (see my previous
                  <a class="ex ju" href="/deep-lucid-dreaming-94fecd3cd46d" rel="noopener">
                   post
                  </a>
                  ) and depth estimation, in addition to integrating everything into an up-to-date PyTorch framework.

There’s a simple goal: To make you familiar and comfortable with the tool, and the language. “Why does it even matter?” I see you asking.                    CatBoost
                  </a>

It beat mainly LightGBM and XGBoost, which have recently been the standard before in not only data science competitions, but also in professional settings as well. Now is the time to learn this powerful library, and below is how you can implement it in four easy steps.

                   <a class="ex ca" href="/the-root-of-all-software-design-challenge-independent-or-dependent-31252051bf0e?source=collection_home---------7----------------------------" rel="noopener">

                  <h1 class="hs ht hn be hu hv hw hx hy hz ia ib ic id ie if ig ih ii ij y il hd" id="c88f">
                   <a class="ex ca" href="/multivariate-outlier-detection-in-python-e946cfc843b3?source=collection_home---------8----------------------------" rel="noopener">
                    Multivariate Outlier Detection in Python
                   </a>
                  </h1>
                 </div>
                 <div class="">
                  <h2 class="im ht hn be b in io ip iq ir is it iu iv iw ix iy iz ej" id="21e4">
                   Multivariate Outliers and Mahalanobis Distance in Python
                  </h2>
                 </div>
                 <p class="jv jw hn jx b iq hw jy is hz jz ka kb kc kd ke kf kg kh ki mq kj hh hd" id="3cdf">
                  Detecting outliers in multivariate data can often be one of the challenges of the data preprocessing phase. There are various distance metrics, scores, and techniques to detect outliers. Euclidean distance is one of the most known distance metrics to identify outliers based on their distance to the center point. There is also a Z-Score to define outliers for a single numeric variable. In some cases, clustering algorithms can be also preferred. All these methods consider outliers from different perspectives. The outliers are found based on one method may not be found by the others as outliers. Therefore, these methods and…
                 </p>

                 <section class="hh hi hj eg hk">
                  <div class="">
                   <h1 class="hs ht hn be hu hv hw hx hy hz ia ib ic id ie if ig ih ii ij y il hd" id="1639">
                    <a class="ex ca" href="/an-ai-agent-learns-to-play-tic-tac-toe-part-3-training-a-q-learning-rl-agent-2871cef2faf0?source=collection_home---------9----------------------------" rel="noopener">
                     An AI agent learns to play tic-tac-toe (part 3): training a Q-learning RL agent
                    </a>
                   </h1>
                  </div>
                  <div class="">
                   <h2 class="im ht hn be b in io ip iq ir is it iu iv iw ix iy iz ej" id="e3cc">
                    <em class="pn">
                     Where we use Q learning to train a reinforcement learning agent to play tic-tac-toe
                    </em>
                   </h2>
                  </div>
                  <p class="jv jw hn jx b iq hw jy is hz jz ka kb kc kd ke kf kg kh ki mq kj hh hd" id="9cb7">
                   <em class="po">
                    This article is part of a series that lets a computer play tic-tac-toe using reinforcement learning. You can find
                   </em>
                   <a class="ex ju" href="https://towardsdatascience.com/tagged/rl-series-paul" rel="noopener">
                    <em class="po">
                     all the articles here
                    </em>
                   </a>
                   <em class="po">
                    . The goal is to provide a complete implementation that you can really pick apart and learn reinforcement learning from. It is probably best to read the articles in order. The article including all the code
                   </em>
                   <a class="ex ju" href="https://github.com/PaulHiemstra/qlearning_paper/blob/master/tictoe_qlearning_paper.ipynb" rel="noopener nofollow">
                    <em class="po">
                     can be found on Github
                    </em>
                   </a>
                   <em class="po">
                    .
                   </em>
                  </p>
                  <h1 class="mr ms hn be mt mu ir hx mv it ia iu iv mw iw ix mx iy iz my mz na hd" id="58e2">
                   Reinforcement Learning recap
                  </h1>
                  <p class="jv jw hn jx b iq hw jy is hz jz ka kb kc kd ke kf kg kh ki nb kj hh hd" id="51c5">
                   In
                   <a class="ex ju" href="/an-ai-agent-plays-tic-tac-toe-part-1-building-the-opponent-to-play-against-bb5af74fded1" rel="noopener">
                    part 1
                   </a>
                   and
                   <a class="ex ju" href="/an-ai-agent-plays-tic-tac-toe-part-2-speeding-up-recursive-functions-using-memoization-97253529aea8" rel="noopener">
                    2
                   </a>
                   of this series we built the opponent for our reinforcement learning (RL) agent, so now we can start working on the actual RL agent itself. …
                  </p>
                 </section>
